In this part we shall mostly look to clean our data, which includes:
address missing/duplicate values, look for outliers, correct data types
, fixing categorical variables, Distribution of variables, Low variance
filter.

\section{0.0 - Importing data}\label{importing-data}

As we can see, we have 81 variables in our data set; 1 ID and 1
salesPrice, 43 categorical and 36 quantitative. Data entries are either
int or char data type.

Price}\label{looking-at-our-target-variable-sales-price}

\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}

\end{Highlighting}

\includegraphics{EDA_files/figure-latex/unnamed-chunk-3-1.pdf}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{multiplier <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{myhist}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{counts }\OperatorTok{/}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{myhist}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{density}
\NormalTok{mydensity <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{density}\NormalTok{(raw_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{SalePrice)}
\NormalTok{mydensity}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{y <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{mydensity}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{y }\OperatorTok{*}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{multiplier[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{]}

\KeywordTok{plot}\NormalTok{(myhist, }\DataTypeTok{xlab =} \StringTok{"Sales Price"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{main =} \StringTok{"Histogram of Sales"}\NormalTok{)}
\KeywordTok{lines}\NormalTok{(mydensity)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\includegraphics{EDA_files/figure-latex/unnamed-chunk-3-2.pdf} We can
see that the average sales price of a house is \$181k, the distribution
of which is skewed to the right. As we can see from the histogram, the
right tail is longer and the mass of the concentration of data is to the
left of the graph, suggesting a positive skew value. The peak also looks
very sharp, assuming a high kurtosis value.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{boxplot}\NormalTok{(raw_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{SalePrice)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\includegraphics{EDA_files/figure-latex/unnamed-chunk-4-1.pdf} We can
see that there are many outlier in the SalePrice. In fact, we can
measure knowing that outliers are classified as values over 3rd Quartile
+ 1.5*(IQR)

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{count =}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{;}
\NormalTok{x =}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{;}
\ControlFlowTok{while}\NormalTok{ (x }\OperatorTok{<}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1461}\NormalTok{) \{}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (raw_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{SalePrice[x] }\OperatorTok{>}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{340000}\NormalTok{)\{}
\NormalTok{    count =}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{count }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}
\NormalTok{  \}}
\NormalTok{  x =}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{x }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1} 
\NormalTok{\}}
\KeywordTok{cat}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Number of Sales that lie as outliers are: "}\NormalTok{, count)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
## Number of Sales that lie as outliers are:  61
\end{verbatim}

look into them.

As we can see, there are missing values for many of the entries. Perhaps
it is better that we look to address missing values in our other 80
variables.

\section{1.1.2 Addressing Nas, missing values in our House
Attributes}\label{addressing-nas-missing-values-in-our-house-attributes}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{# Counting number of nulls in each col}
\NormalTok{x =}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}
\KeywordTok{cat}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"---NULL COUNT---}\CharTok{\textbackslash{}n}\StringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
## ---NULL COUNT---
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ControlFlowTok{while}\NormalTok{ (x}\OperatorTok{<}\DecValTok{81}\NormalTok{)\{}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{((raw_data[x]))}\OperatorTok{>}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{))\{}
    \KeywordTok{cat}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Number of nulls in "}\NormalTok{,(}\KeywordTok{colnames}\NormalTok{(raw_data[x])), }\StringTok{": "}\NormalTok{)}
    \KeywordTok{cat}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{sum}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(raw_data[x])), }\StringTok{"}\CharTok{\textbackslash{}n}\StringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{  \}}
\NormalTok{  x =}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{x }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1} 
\NormalTok{\}}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
## Number of nulls in  LotFrontage : 259 
## Number of nulls in  Alley : 1369 
## Number of nulls in  MasVnrType : 8 
## Number of nulls in  MasVnrArea : 8 
## Number of nulls in  BsmtQual : 37 
## Number of nulls in  BsmtCond : 37 
## Number of nulls in  BsmtExposure : 38 
## Number of nulls in  BsmtFinType1 : 37 
## Number of nulls in  BsmtFinType2 : 38 
## Number of nulls in  Electrical : 1 
## Number of nulls in  FireplaceQu : 690 
## Number of nulls in  GarageType : 81 
## Number of nulls in  GarageYrBlt : 81 
## Number of nulls in  GarageFinish : 81 
## Number of nulls in  GarageQual : 81 
## Number of nulls in  GarageCond : 81 
## Number of nulls in  PoolQC : 1453 
## Number of nulls in  Fence : 1179 
## Number of nulls in  MiscFeature : 1406
\end{verbatim}

There are 19 variables with NA values. It is important to note that this
might mean that the observation is missing or perhaps a NA means
somthing itself. We must consult the data dictionary.

LotFrontage has 259 NA values. This is integer value repersenting Linear
feet of street connected to property. Looking into the dataset, we see
that the other observations have a value anywhere from 21-313. We can
safetly assume that these 259 entries repersent a house that has 0
linear feet of street being connected to the property. Of course it
could be a case of missin value, but it is possible that the homes do
not have the property connecting to a steet, we take this assumptions
and instead change the NAs to 0. As such, We will not be removing such
observations

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{v =}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}
\ControlFlowTok{while}\NormalTok{ (v}\OperatorTok{<}\DecValTok{1461}\NormalTok{)\{}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{LotFrontage[v]))\{}
\NormalTok{    modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{LotFrontage[v] =}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{0}
\NormalTok{  \}}
\NormalTok{  v =}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{v }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}
\NormalTok{\}}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Alley has 1369 NAs, this high number suggests that the NAs must mean
somthing rather than missing value. The dictionary shows us the NA
repersents no alley Access. Rather than Na, lets change that to `None' a
bit more repersentative.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{v =}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}
\ControlFlowTok{while}\NormalTok{ (v}\OperatorTok{<}\DecValTok{1461}\NormalTok{)\{}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{Alley[v]))\{}
\NormalTok{    modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{Alley[v] =}\StringTok{ "None"}
\NormalTok{  \}}
\NormalTok{  v =}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{v }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}
\NormalTok{\}}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

MasVnrType and MasVnrArea both have 8 missing values. This is very
suspeious. Could it be that they are of the same observations and due to
another house feature? Let us check. Maybe our data dictionary can help
us with this.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{MasVnr <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{subset}\NormalTok{(raw_data, }\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(raw_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{MasVnrType))}
\NormalTok{MasVnr}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{Area <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{subset}\NormalTok{(raw_data, }\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(raw_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{MasVnrArea))}
\NormalTok{MasVnr}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

These both variables are Na in the same observation. What is weird is
that MasVnrType has a None category, so that means that it isn't a case
that there was no masonry veneer, rather I would say that the Masonry
data was not collected for these 8 observations. This would tell me that
it might be good to remove the observations

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{modified_data <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{subset}\NormalTok{(modified_data, }\OperatorTok{!}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(raw_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{MasVnrType)) }\CommentTok{# we only do it for when one attribute isnt na, because the other overlaps.}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Next lets look at BsmtQual, BsmtCond, BsmtExposure, BsmtFinType1,
BsmtFinType2. All these have 37-38 missing values. Lets see if they are
overlapping observations again, and see if we can figure out a pattern.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{Bsmt <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{subset}\NormalTok{(raw_data, }\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(raw_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtExposure))}
\NormalTok{Bsmt}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Here we can see that they all overlap and there is a pattern here. They
are all basement, perhaps there is somthing odd about the basement.
Looking in the data dictionary confirms our suspicions, NA repersents No
basements for all of there variables. These are not missing values, and
NA is a very meaningful entry. I don't like the use of NA, I would
rather use a more descriptive categorical name: NoB

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{v =}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}
\ControlFlowTok{while}\NormalTok{ (v}\OperatorTok{<}\DecValTok{1453}\NormalTok{)\{}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtQual[v]))\{}
\NormalTok{    modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtQual[v] =}\StringTok{ "NoB"}
\NormalTok{  \}}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtCond[v]))\{}
\NormalTok{    modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtCond[v] =}\StringTok{ "NoB"}
\NormalTok{  \}}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtExposure[v]))\{}
\NormalTok{    modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtExposure[v] =}\StringTok{ "NoB"}
\NormalTok{  \}}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtFinType1[v]))\{}
\NormalTok{    modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtFinType1[v] =}\StringTok{ "NoB"}
\NormalTok{  \}}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtFinType2[v]))\{}
\NormalTok{    modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtFinType2[v] =}\StringTok{ "NoB"}
\NormalTok{  \}}
\NormalTok{  v =}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{v }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}
\NormalTok{\}}
\NormalTok{Bsmt1 <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{subset}\NormalTok{(modified_data, modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtExposure }\OperatorTok{==}\StringTok{ "NoB"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{Bsmt1}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

It's important to note that observation 949 has a basement that is
unfinished and the Exposure is set to NA. This is a potential missing
value, only because we know that the other categorical variables label
this observation as UNFINSHED rather than NO BASEMENT. The exposture
could have been set at No exposure, but rather was set to a level
repersenting no basement. I think it's safe to remove this data
observation.

Also observation 333 has a signular basement with FinType2 as NA.
FinType1 does have a value, however, and after looking through other
observations, this stikes as very odd. FinType repersents the finishing
of the basement, FinType1 repersents the first layer, and FinType2
repersents any additional layers (if there are any), however in the
event there is one layer, other entries would have FinType2 as UNF or No
Basement. I think it is safe to eliminate this observation.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{modified_data <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{modified_data[}\OperatorTok{-}\KeywordTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{949}\NormalTok{),]}
\NormalTok{modified_data <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{modified_data[}\OperatorTok{-}\KeywordTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{333}\NormalTok{),]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Poof! The two records are gone.

For the misisng electrical data, we will be removing it, because NA has
no meaning behind it and there needs to be an option for it.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{modified_data <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{subset}\NormalTok{(modified_data, }\OperatorTok{!}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{Electrical))}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Poof! It's gone!

For FireplaceQu, I looked ahead at the data dictionary, and it clearly
states all NAs means no Fireplace, so we can attribute this to a better
categorical variable: NoF

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{v =}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}
\ControlFlowTok{while}\NormalTok{ (v}\OperatorTok{<}\DecValTok{1450}\NormalTok{)\{}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{FireplaceQu[v]))\{}
\NormalTok{    modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{FireplaceQu[v] =}\StringTok{ "NoF"}
\NormalTok{  \}}
\NormalTok{  v =}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{v }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}
\NormalTok{\}}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

And now again we have 5 variables that describe the same part of the
house, the garage (GarageType, GarageYrBlt, GarageFinish, GarageQual,
GarageCond), and they have equal amounts of NA (81). And to no suprise,
NA for each of those variables means No garage. We'll chnage this to NoG
instead.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{v =}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}
\ControlFlowTok{while}\NormalTok{ (v}\OperatorTok{<}\DecValTok{1450}\NormalTok{)\{}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{GarageType[v]))\{}
\NormalTok{    modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{GarageType[v] =}\StringTok{ "NoG"}
\NormalTok{  \}}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{GarageYrBlt[v]))\{}
\NormalTok{    modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{GarageYrBlt[v] =}\StringTok{ "NoG"}
\NormalTok{  \}}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{GarageFinish[v]))\{}
\NormalTok{    modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{GarageFinish[v] =}\StringTok{ "NoG"}
\NormalTok{  \}}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{GarageQual[v]))\{}
\NormalTok{    modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{GarageQual[v] =}\StringTok{ "NoG"}
\NormalTok{  \}}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{GarageCond[v]))\{}
\NormalTok{    modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{GarageCond[v] =}\StringTok{ "NoG"}
\NormalTok{  \}}
\NormalTok{  v =}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{v }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}
\NormalTok{\}}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

I found it that the next three attributes had a lot of NA entires. So I
looked into the data dictionary, they all repersent the missing item for
the attribute. They are not missing values, so will not be excluded, but
given better names. NA for PoolQc will be chnaged to NoP, NA for Fence
will be NoF, and NA for MiscFeature will become NoM.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{v =}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}
\ControlFlowTok{while}\NormalTok{ (v}\OperatorTok{<}\DecValTok{1450}\NormalTok{)\{}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{PoolQC[v]))\{}
\NormalTok{    modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{PoolQC[v] =}\StringTok{ "NoP"}
\NormalTok{  \}}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{Fence[v]))\{}
\NormalTok{    modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{Fence[v] =}\StringTok{ "NoF"}
\NormalTok{  \}}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.na}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{MiscFeature[v]))\{}
\NormalTok{    modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{MiscFeature[v] =}\StringTok{ "NoM"}
\NormalTok{  \}}
\NormalTok{  v =}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{v }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}
\NormalTok{\}}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

We should be done will addressing missing values, lets check!

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{x =}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}

\NormalTok{colname <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{colnames}\NormalTok{(modified_data)}
\NormalTok{temp =}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{modified_data}
\CommentTok{#remeber which attributes to remove}
\NormalTok{toremove =}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{as.vector}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{outers=}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{as.vector}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{)}

\end{Highlighting}

This will be a strainious process, but I will be going thru each
variable. we shall see if there is a need to reduce the levels for the
categorical ones, and if outliers need to be dealt with for the
numerical ones.

\begin{Highlighting}[]

be removed.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]

\NormalTok{colname[attrib]}

\begin{verbatim}
## [1] "MSSubClass"
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{typeof}\NormalTok{(temp[,attrib]) }\OperatorTok{==}\StringTok{ 'integer'}\NormalTok{)\{}
\NormalTok{graph =}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{boxplot}\NormalTok{(temp[,attrib])}
\KeywordTok{length}\NormalTok{(graph}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{out)}
\NormalTok{graph}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{out}
\NormalTok{outlierID =}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{which}\NormalTok{(temp[,attrib]}\OperatorTok{>}\NormalTok{graph}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{stats[}\DecValTok{5}\NormalTok{],)}
\NormalTok{temp[outlierID,]}
\NormalTok{\}}

\ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{typeof}\NormalTok{(temp[,attrib]) }\OperatorTok{==}\StringTok{ 'character'}\NormalTok{)\{}
\KeywordTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{as.data.frame}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{table}\NormalTok{(temp[,attrib])))}
\KeywordTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{ggplot}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{data =}\NormalTok{ temp, }\KeywordTok{aes}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{x=}\NormalTok{temp[,attrib], }\DataTypeTok{y=}\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{SalePrice)) }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{geom_boxplot}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{aes}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{fill =} \KeywordTok{factor}\NormalTok{(temp[,attrib]) )) }\OperatorTok{+}\KeywordTok{scale_x_discrete}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{name =}\NormalTok{ (colname[attrib])) }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{labs}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{fill =}\NormalTok{ (colname[attrib])))}

There is no reason for us to be chnaging this. Changing to quality
ranges would not help the distribution (ex 1-3, 4-7, 8-10). Will keep as
is.

\KeywordTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{ggplot}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{data =}\NormalTok{ temp, }\KeywordTok{aes}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{x=}\NormalTok{temp[,attrib], }\DataTypeTok{y=}\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{SalePrice)) }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{geom_boxplot}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{aes}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{fill =} \KeywordTok{factor}\NormalTok{(temp[,attrib]) )) }\OperatorTok{+}\KeywordTok{scale_x_discrete}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{name =}\NormalTok{ (colname[attrib])) }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{labs}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{fill =}\NormalTok{ (colname[attrib])))}

\NormalTok{global =}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{global }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}
\NormalTok{toremove[global] =}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{attrib}
\NormalTok{\}}
\end{Highlighting}

\section{1.1.5 Low variance Filter and correlation of our numeric
attributes, outlier handling and Feature
engineering}\label{low-variance-filter-and-correlation-of-our-numeric-attributes-outlier-handling-and-feature-engineering}

We will be working on checking the vairance of each variable. We want
high variance.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{#The ruleset I am emplaying is if there is one variable with over 65% of the observations or 2 with over 70%, I shall remove the attribute based of low variance.  }
\NormalTok{temp[toremove] <-}\StringTok{ }\OtherTok{NULL}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

We shall look at the matrix of the numeric attributes and remove any
that have higher than 0.75 correlation with the dependent variable

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{#Subsetting for numeric only}
\NormalTok{nums <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{unlist}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{lapply}\NormalTok{(temp, is.numeric))}
\NormalTok{numONLY =}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{temp[,nums]}
\NormalTok{aa<-}\KeywordTok{cor}\NormalTok{(numONLY)}
\KeywordTok{ggcorrplot}\NormalTok{(aa)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

There are some conclusions we can make.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{#Might be better for us to remove 4 attributes and create a fuller 1 attribute}
\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{HouseArea <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{TotalBsmtSF }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{X1stFlrSF }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{X2ndFlrSF}

\CommentTok{# Undo some work from before for this stage.}
\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{FullBath <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{as.numeric}\NormalTok{(temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{FullBath)}
\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtFullBath <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{as.numeric}\NormalTok{(temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtFullBath)}
\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{HalfBath <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{as.numeric}\NormalTok{(temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{HalfBath)}
\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtHalfBath <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{as.numeric}\NormalTok{(temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtHalfBath)}

\CommentTok{# Why keep so many bathroom attributes. Let us condense instead.}
\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{TotalBath <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{FullBath }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\FloatTok{0.5}\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{(temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{HalfBath) }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtFullBath }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\FloatTok{0.5}\OperatorTok{*}\KeywordTok{as.numeric}\NormalTok{(temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{BsmtHalfBath)}
\CommentTok{# Same with porch}
\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{TotalPorchSF <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{OpenPorchSF }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{EnclosedPorch }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{X3SsnPorch }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{ScreenPorch }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{WoodDeckSF}
\CommentTok{# Lets include the garage now}
\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{TotalArea <-temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{HouseArea }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{GarageArea}
\CommentTok{#We also know that total basement SF = BsmtFinSF1 + BsmtFinSF2 + BsmtUnfSF. WHy not remove it }
\CommentTok{#Another reason so remove total basement SF is because of its high correlation to 1stFlrSF}
\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{TotalBsmtSF <-}\StringTok{ }\OtherTok{NULL}
\CommentTok{#Do not need house area, if we have total area}
\NormalTok{temp}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{HouseArea <-}\StringTok{ }\OtherTok{NULL}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

We will remove OverallQual and GrLiveArea due to its high correlation.
(above our 0.7 threshold) GarageCars and Garagearea also have high
correlation, and they themselves are highly correlated (0.88), so I
shall remove one because they pretty much provide the same amount of
information to the dependent variable. I pick Garagearea to remove
because there are already a lot of area variables.

Also lets remove the attributes used in the addition, as well.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]

\section{1.3 Remove those outlier!}\label{remove-those-outlier}

I saved this for as late as possible. I wanted to see if most of the
attributes will be eliminated before we remove observations due to
outliers.

\section{2 - EDA}\label{eda}

\section{2.1 Normalization}\label{normalization}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{# Our Normalizing technique}
\NormalTok{normalize <-}\StringTok{ }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x) \{}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.numeric}\NormalTok{(x))\{}
  \KeywordTok{return}\NormalTok{ ((x }\OperatorTok{-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{min}\NormalTok{(x)) }\OperatorTok{/}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{max}\NormalTok{(x) }\OperatorTok{-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{min}\NormalTok{(x))) \}}
  \ControlFlowTok{else}\NormalTok{\{}
    \KeywordTok{return}\NormalTok{ (x)}
\NormalTok{  \}}
\NormalTok{\}}
\NormalTok{data_norm =}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{as.data.frame}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{lapply}\NormalTok{(modified_data[}\DecValTok{2}\OperatorTok{:}\DecValTok{39}\NormalTok{], normalize))}
\NormalTok{data_norm <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{cbind}\NormalTok{(modified_data}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{SalePrice, data_norm)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{# It is not meaningful to have clustering for categorical variables. I did only numerical values.}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

In fact, these clusters are not meaningful for the numerical only
attributes, either! It would have been a better tool to be used in EDA
of 2-5 variables perhaps, but I will do without it.

\begin{Shaded}

\CommentTok{#Splitting training to 80%, test to 20%}
\NormalTok{index <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{sample}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{1}\OperatorTok{:}\KeywordTok{nrow}\NormalTok{(data_norm), }\FloatTok{0.80} \OperatorTok{*}\KeywordTok{nrow}\NormalTok{(data_norm))}
\NormalTok{data_train <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{data_norm[index,]}
\NormalTok{data_test <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{data_norm[}\OperatorTok{-}\NormalTok{index,]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Learned that KNN might not be a good suit for someone with categorical
data within the DF. We shall need to look at regression.
